## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and current concentration. Classical rate laws relate reaction rates to powers of concentration, and more complex mechanisms (enzymatic, autocatalytic, reversible) introduce rational or product forms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, simple decomposition)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law kinetics)
- First-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (reversible first-order reaction approaching equilibrium)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (competing reaction pathways)
- Second-order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate with back-reaction)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Exponential decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * A) (concentration-dependent activation energy)
- Combined time and concentration: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or aging kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple power-law dependence on concentration (dA/dt ~ A^n) suggests an elementary reaction of order n; integer orders (0,1,2) are most common for elementary steps
- A rate expression that is a polynomial in A (e.g., quadratic) often indicates a reversible reaction or competing parallel reactions
- Rational functions of A (numerator/denominator both involving A) suggest enzyme kinetics or surface-catalyzed reactions with adsorption-desorption equilibria
- Product form A*(c-A) indicates autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics where the species both catalyzes and is consumed
- Explicit time dependence beyond what is captured through A(t) suggests non-isothermal conditions, photochemical forcing, or catalyst deactivation
- Negative values of dA/dt with magnitude increasing with A indicate consumption kinetics; sign reversal at specific A values indicates equilibrium
- Square root dependence (A**0.5) can arise from chain reaction mechanisms or dissociative equilibria preceding the rate-limiting step
- Exponential dependence on A (exp(c*A)) may arise from concentration-dependent changes in activation energy or ionic strength effects
